# Relevant Policy Document URL: 
# This document describes the Internationalized Domain Names (IDN) Character Table used by Amazon Registry Services, Inc. within the xn--fct429k registry for the registration of xn--fct429k domains in the Japanese language. 
# {RO}’s Japanese IDN implementation has a feature that mitigates homographic attacks due to Han variants by blocking a name from being registered if a similar name is already registered.  
# This feature works looks at every registered # domain name and compares it to a computed canonical string associated with it.  This canonical string is only used registry-internally to block 
# similar names from being registered. 
# The table below lists the characters allowed for registration under the "jp" language tag in the first column. The second column shows the canonical codepoint corresponding to the first 
# column. Due to the differences between this table and the xn--fct429k Chinese language table, some characters in the second column of this table may not appear in the first column at all.  However, 
# this should not affect registrars as the second column is only used internally by the registry and provided as a reference. Additionally, since every character in the xn--fct429k registry is an independent 
# entity with no contextual restrictions, our implementation excludes context-sensitive codepoints, such as U+30FC;U+4E00 (# KATAKANA-HIRAGANA PROLONGED SOUND MARK ー;一) 
# which requires an addition of co-locational constraints that are not inherent to the xn--fct429k registry. This means that registration of any domain name containing this character will fail. Our feeling 
# is that the benefits of excluding the few context-sensitive characters far outweigh what is lost by not having them.
# This table is in compliance with the ICANN Guidelines for the Implementation of Internationalized Domain Names and is intended for publication in the IANA IDN Character Table Registry.
#
